  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_593b2425-d64a-47a2-b370-bbbf38d2649a'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer17670886316673385959">Annith has watched her gifted sisters at the convent come and go, carrying out their dark dealings in the name of St. Mortain, patiently awaiting her own turn to serve Death.   <span id="freeText17670886316673385959" style="display:none">Annith has watched her gifted sisters at the convent come and go, carrying out their dark dealings in the name of St. Mortain, patiently awaiting her own turn to serve Death. But her worst fears are realized when she discovers she is being groomed by the abbess as a Seeress, to be forever sequestered in the rock and stone womb of the convent. Feeling sorely betrayed, Annith decides to strike out on her own.<br /><br />She has spent her whole life training to be an assassin. Just because the convent has changed its mind doesn't mean she has...</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer131632622293846005"><b> 3.5 stars </b><br/><br/><b> <i> “If Death could grant you a wish, you would use it for someone else? Trade your happiness for someone else's?” </i> </b><br/><br/><a href='http://s177.photobucket.com/user/dawnygirl07/media/mortalheart.png.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421394112i/13370906.png' alt=' photo mortalheart.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b> As I always do with my 3 star reviews, I maintain that just because I rated a book 3 stars does not mean I didn't like it/it isn't good. I enjoyed this book, but not as much as the two books before it. Therefore, 3 stars. </b><br/><br/>I truly believe that Robin LaFevers has brought something special to the young adult genre with her His Fair Assassin trilogy. I can't recall a hist</span>
  <span id="freeText131632622293846005" style="display:none"><b> 3.5 stars </b><br><br><b> <i> “If Death could grant you a wish, you would use it for someone else? Trade your happiness for someone else's?” </i> </b><br><br><a href="http://s177.photobucket.com/user/dawnygirl07/media/mortalheart.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421394112i/13370906.png" alt=" photo mortalheart.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b> As I always do with my 3 star reviews, I maintain that just because I rated a book 3 stars does not mean I didn't like it/it isn't good. I enjoyed this book, but not as much as the two books before it. Therefore, 3 stars. </b><br><br>I truly believe that Robin LaFevers has brought something special to the young adult genre with her His Fair Assassin trilogy. I can't recall a historical fiction book(s) within this genre that has been so beautifully executed with strong female characters. That being said, Mortal Heart is probably my least favorite book in this series, the second book Dark Triumph the best. <br><br>Mortal Heart is Annith's story. We know her from the previous books, as she is friend and sister to Ismae and Sybella. Unlike the other girls, Annith has spent her life in the convent since birth. Annith has been waiting and longing for years to be sent out on an assignment, like her sisters before her. One day while spying on the Reverend Mother, Annith discovers that she is not meant to leave the convent, but to stay forever and be the next Seeress. Finding this a horrible fate, Annith strikes out on her own after the Reverend Mother to demand answers as to her fate.<br><br><a href="http://s177.photobucket.com/user/dawnygirl07/media/ivyseparator.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421394112i/13370907.png" alt=" photo ivyseparator.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Being that this book is almost 450 pages, it was really a sad fact that it took almost 100 pages in for the book to finally grasp my undivided attention. In my opinion this book was pretty darn scattered, with Annith doing one thing but then getting roped into other journey next. For example, when she leaves the convent with a set course but then ends up with the Helliquin, and then the women warriors. It just felt a little jumbled in my opinion. The plot at times was very straightforward, but really only when it pertained to the political plot with the Duchess. I felt that it was not consistent when it came to Annith's plot.<br><br>I liked the addition of the helliquin and Balthazaar to the series; he was a very interesting and mysterious character and remained so throughout the entire book. The connection (romantically and otherwise) between him and Annith was a bit difficult to believe at the beginning, but near the end of the book it made a lot more sense.<br><br><b> <i> “I am beginning to think that love itself is never wrong. It is what love can drive people to do that is the problem.” </i> </b> <br><br>I enjoyed the fact that we got to see a bit more of Ismae and Sybella, and a part of my wishes that the author would write some epilogue novellas for them. It felt to me like the stories of the 3 main girls remains largely unfinished.<br><br>I also liked the resolution of the Duchess's struggles. After 3 books of trying to find a solution I believe the author found a very inventive and creative end to her story. I'm also kind of hoping for the Duchess to get her own book.<br><br>Strong end to a strong series, but not my favorite book of the 3. <br><br><b> <i> “We are all of us, gods and mortals, made up of many pieces, some of them broken, some of them scarred, but none of them the total sum of who we are.” </i> </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="131632622293846005" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1728230962" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer1283914995894577942">I felt sorry for Annith for a good part of the book. All she wanted was to go out and do her duty and serve Death (Mortain) but she has been kept at the convent. She can't understand why, as the best assassin they have, that she is being kept and not sent out on missions. Yeah, I never saw that reason coming, not for a long shot. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471309199i/20024869._SX540_.jpg' alt=' : ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Annith misses Ismae and Sybella from the first two books so much and she can't understand why she is still at the convent and not helping them. I already said that, but</span>
  <span id="freeText1283914995894577942" style="display:none">I felt sorry for Annith for a good part of the book. All she wanted was to go out and do her duty and serve Death (Mortain) but she has been kept at the convent. She can't understand why, as the best assassin they have, that she is being kept and not sent out on missions. Yeah, I never saw that reason coming, not for a long shot. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471309199i/20024869._SX540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Annith misses Ismae and Sybella from the first two books so much and she can't understand why she is still at the convent and not helping them. I already said that, but still. She's just really sad and down on herself. <br><br><b>I cannot help it--I laugh. "You think you can best me?"<br>She lifts one shoulder. "I think I would like to know if I could or could not."<br>At her words, my smile wobbles and it is all I can do to keep from throwing my knife down in defeat. Even this child thinks I am not longer a match for her. I carefully avoid looking out at the ocean, just beyond the trees. It is too painful a reminder that both Ismae and Sybella have been sent places I have not, have begun to fulfill their destinies while I am stuck here playing nursemaid to a gaggle of budding assassins.</b><br><br>When Annith learns of what the abbess wants her to become she decides to set out on her own. She runs into some interesting people on the way to her destination. One would be the hellequins &lt;--- I hope I spelled that right. They are immortals that basically go around and get lost souls to cross over and they are a rough bunch. They are trying to redeem themselves of bad things they had done in their past lives. <br><br>Annith meets Balthazaar, the leader of the hellequins and they have some chemistry. I thought he was hot, just sayin. <br><br>Then Annith gets some things into her head and runs away and ends up meeting a group of warrior women called the Arduinnites. They were really nice to her but they brought some really sad news to Annith and now she is on a mission to kill. <br><br>Annith finally makes it to Sybella and Ismae, she tells them of some things she thinks is peculiar in the covent. Something is up with the abbess and it's more than I would have thought. That was a pretty deep revelation when I got to it. <br><br>And in this book we also find out more about Mortain and who he really is and OMG, I loved it! It was one of those holy crow moments that everyone else probably figured out but me! <br><br>Either way, I enjoyed all of the books in this trilogy! How often do you read about bad to the bone butt kicking nuns that will take you out? <br><br>MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2016/08/mortal-heart-by-robin-lafevers.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a></span>

<div id="review_1359105255" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1359105255" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1720620-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415374035p2/1720620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1359105255" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7292094698906361412">3.5 stars<br/><br/>Not a bad finish for this trilogy, but it was a bit too long for my taste. There just wasn't enough action to keep me interested in this 444 page book. By the 60% mark, I was checking in earnest to see how much longer till <b>Mortal Heart</b> wrapped up.<br/>It wasn't boring, per say, it just got kinda draggy.<br/><br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441126345ra/16066428.gif' width='400' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Also, I had already figured out the 3 Big Reveals, and I was sort of just waiting on the end of the book for confirmation.<br/><i>Pssst. I was right about all of them.</i><br/>And, you know, that's just a bum</span>
  <span id="freeText7292094698906361412" style="display:none">3.5 stars<br><br>Not a bad finish for this trilogy, but it was a bit too long for my taste. There just wasn't enough action to keep me interested in this 444 page book. By the 60% mark, I was checking in earnest to see how much longer till <b>Mortal Heart</b> wrapped up.<br>It wasn't boring, per say, it just got kinda draggy.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441126345ra/16066428.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Also, I had already figured out the 3 Big Reveals, and I was sort of just waiting on the end of the book for confirmation.<br><i>Pssst. I was right about all of them.</i><br>And, you know, that's just a bummer. I hate it when nothing surprises me, because then I end up feeling sort of blah about the whole book. Not horrible, mind you, just<i> meh</i>.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441126416ra/16066429.gif" width="350" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ok, so this is Annith's story, but the ladies from the other 2 books make appearances, as well. I thought that their additions to the story were very well done. This being the last book, it tied up all the loose ends, so having the 3 of them meet up and finish everything off together was great.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441126565ra/16066438.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>How was the romance?<br>Well, it was alright. It didn't start off with insta-love on Annith's part, and it was nice to see a woman who wasn't fawning all over the first guy to pay her any attention.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441126750ra/16066464.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I mean, he <i>
  <b>was</b>
</i> quite literally the first guy she had ever really had any real contact with. So, it would have been pretty easy for the author to make her go all doe-eyed &amp; weak in the knees over him. But since she didn't get stupid over him in the beginning, I kinda enjoyed the lovey-dovey stuff. And by the end of the book, when they were going pretty hot an heavy, it felt more natural than I expected due to <b>{spoilery reasons}</b>. Also, it was all pretty fade to black, so while there <i>was</i> sex, you're not getting anything graphic.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441126832ra/16066472.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Final Book = Final Battle</b><br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441126884ra/16066479.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So, how was it?<br>Well, considering how much the book seemed to drag on in parts, I thought the end was pretty good. There was enough of that<i>
  <b> OhMyGodWillEveryoneMakeIt!?</b>
</i> kind of thing going on to keep my ass riveted to the seat. And once it was over, LaFevers tied up all of the loose plot threads quite nicely.<br>Or, at least, I<i> think</i> she did.<br>I haven't read the second book yet (still on hold at my library!), but it looked to me like everyone &amp; everything got a tidy ending. And while I wasn't blown out of the water by this one, I'm still glad I read it, if for no other reason than (after I get my hands on book 2!) I can finally tick this trilogy off my list.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441126973ra/16066493.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Also reviewed for:<br><div>
  <a href="http://www.addicted2heroines.com/2015/09/review-mortal-heart-his-fair-assassin-3.html" title="Addicted 2 Heroines" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1412937777i/11444542.jpg" alt="Addicted 2 Heroines" width="100%" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div></span>

<div id="review_1483315328" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Maggie ☘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40477684-maggie"><img alt="Maggie ☘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591529603p2/40477684.jpg" /></a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone who loved previous two books</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=intriguing-world-building">intriguing-world-building</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=amazing-reads">amazing-reads</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1483315328" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10900097969355839388">*4/5 stars*<br/><br/><b>
  <i>“We are all of us, gods and mortals, made up of many pieces, some of them broken, some of them scarred, but none of them the total sum of who we are.”</i>
</b><br/><br/><br/><i>Mortal Heart</i>, the last book from <i>His Fair Assassin trilogy </i> is a great conclusion to the His Fair Assassin trilogy, although in comparison to the other two novels, my least favourite. Wich is not to say I didn't enjoy it, I simply wasn't as in love with it - and the main heorine - as in the first two books.<br/><br/><br/>The story is heavier on rom</span>
  <span id="freeText10900097969355839388" style="display:none">*4/5 stars*<br><br><b>
  <i>“We are all of us, gods and mortals, made up of many pieces, some of them broken, some of them scarred, but none of them the total sum of who we are.”</i>
</b><br><br><br><i>Mortal Heart</i>, the last book from <i>His Fair Assassin trilogy </i> is a great conclusion to the His Fair Assassin trilogy, although in comparison to the other two novels, my least favourite. Wich is not to say I didn't enjoy it, I simply wasn't as in love with it - and the main heorine - as in the first two books.<br><br><br>The story is heavier on romance, as well as slower at parts. It also contains more supernatural elements than the previous two books - readers finally discover more about the gods, Mortain and also the Hellequin, His damned vassals. The plot is a bit slower in comparison to book two. It did took me a bit longer to finish than Dark Triumph.<br><br><br><b><i>“You cannot turn a wolf into a lap dog.”</i> - Ismae</b><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451324524i/17528081.jpg" width="240" height="330" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Annith lived her entire life in convent of St. Mortain and longed to be sent on assignment and serve as Mortain's handmaiden. She tried to be nice and obedient for fear of being punished and rejected. She needed to excell in everything, be the best in every skill taught in the convent, but underneath it all felt uncertain about her worth as His handmaiden. Why wasn't she sent out on assignment already. She is the best fighter, excels in horsemanship and archery. Then why did the abbess send Sybella and Ismae after just a few years of training, but not her. There's something deeply wrong with the convent and it's abbess.<br><br><br><b>
  <i>“I realize now, now that it has been taken away from me, that the only thing that kept me from despair all these years was the belief that one day I would finally be able to get off this island—this place where I have had to guard every thought, hide every true feeling, and weigh every gesture. It was the promise of having a life of my own—away from the convent—that fueled my determination to excel at everything they threw at me.”</i>
</b><br><br><br>When the abbess decides that Annith would make the perfect Seeress - thus would stay locked and oppressed in the convent for the rest of her life - and sends out on dangerous assignment young unprepared girl, Annith decides to finally take matters in her hands and leave, even if it means defy Mortain Himself.<br><br>On the way to the duchess, Annith encounters a group of Hellequin. Uncertain and afraid of what tho do, she accepts an offer from Balthazaar - dark, brooding leader of the Hellequin - and decides to hide in their midst.<br><br><br><b><i>“If you so much as snicker, I will kill you all.”</i> - Balthazaar</b><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1551283981i/27126058._SX540_.jpg" width="370" height="270" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>The main issue for me - and the reason as to why I didn't give it 5 stars - is that Annith is my least favourite heroine of the three. Don't get me wrong, I did like her and still think she's much better than a lot of other YA heroines, but I also thought she was rather on the nice, but bland side in comparison to the other two. Maybe partly due to her upbringing, and how different it was to Ismae and Sybella. It didn't harden her as much. I also really liked Balthazaar's character, although the romantic aspect was as well my least favorite - I did prefer Sybella and Beast, and then Ismae and Duval. Still, I can't bring myself to give this book less than four stars.<br><br><br><b>
  <i>“I am beginning to think that love itself is never wrong. It is what love can drive people to do that is the problem.”</i>
</b><br><br><br>There's something <b>dark</b>, <b>uncanny</b> and <b>magical</b> about this trilogy. The prose is gorgeous, <b>each main heroine is completely different </b> and the story <b>nicely combines fictional characters with true historical events</b>.<br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1551279220i/27125714._SY540_.jpg" width="250" height="390" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>All in all, <i>Mortal Heart </i> is satisfying ending to the trilogy with some very surprising twists (especially one particular thing!!!), I know what would each heroine do for a few years, but still will remain hopeful for some sequel from this amazing world. P.S. Which we are getting in the form of Courting Darkness!<br><br><br><b>
  <i>“And so I find myself telling my story for Sybella while she dresses. By the time I am done, she is smiling at me with pride, as if she herself had been responsible for my daring. Which—I realize with a jolt of understanding—she partially is. In giving me love, Ismae and Sybella have given me strength.”</i>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="10900097969355839388" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <i>His Fair Assassin</i>
</b> trilogy by Robin LaFevers. I am not the biggest fan of fantasy novels and even less of historical setting, but I picked these books up by sheer luck. Best decision ever because stories about Ismae and Sybella have everything that I love - great premise, strong female characters, political intrigue and enough of romance to make everything interesting. <br/><br/> <b>I was sca</b></span>
  <span id="freeText15646077865595094712" style="display:none"><b>Review posted at <a href="http://jacitamati.blogspot.com/2014/12/mortal-heart-his-fair-assassin-3-by.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Ja čitam, a ti?</a></b><br><br> One of the biggest surprises for me this year was discovery of absolutely amazing <b>
  <i>His Fair Assassin</i>
</b> trilogy by Robin LaFevers. I am not the biggest fan of fantasy novels and even less of historical setting, but I picked these books up by sheer luck. Best decision ever because stories about Ismae and Sybella have everything that I love - great premise, strong female characters, political intrigue and enough of romance to make everything interesting. <br><br> <b>I was scared to read Mortal Heart.</b> Previous two books had few similar things when it comes to the story, but still each was original and thrilling to read. My biggest fear about Mortal Heart was just that - will it manage to be fresh, new story or it will turn into repetitive pattern. Once again, I was left speechless. Holy Mortain, what a twist! I did not see that coming. Well, I did guessed in the very end, but even then I wan't completely sure.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1417452009ra/12363010.gif" width="500" height="219" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> <b>Medieval biker gang and damsel in distress (who doesn't need a prince to save her).</b> I was swooning and laughing so hard because I couldn't stop comparing Balthazaar and his... gang? crew?... how ever you want to call them, with all my favorite fictional biker boys. They are savages, cruel and intimidating, riding big, scary horses and going all "alpha males" in front of Annith. I loved every second of it.<br><br> <b>Nicely wrapped up.</b> I was wondering how will some of the aspects of the trilogy be explained or end (again one of the things that scared me), but I shouldn't have any doubts. I have to keep my mouth shut - spoilers, you know - but I can't wait to see what you will think about the way this book ended.<br> <br>Check out my reviews for the other books in this series:<br><b>

<div id="review_546032393" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/546032393" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/546032393?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=fantastic-fantasy">fantastic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=book-boyfriend-material">book-boyfriend-material</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=chick-i-want-to-hang-out-with">chick-i-want-to-hang-out-with</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer546032393" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2330784981217602559">One of the things that I have liked so much about the His Fair Assassins series, besides the Assassin Nuns of course is the <b>blending of completely fictionalized characters with actual historical events</b>. The time lines are not exact but the major events and characters are. <br/><br/>Grave Mercy was more of a political intrigue, Dark Triumph an Adventure and now Mortal Heart is more of a Fantasy and love story. This book is far more invested into the lore of the gods Mortain in particular but the other Nine</span>
  <span id="freeText2330784981217602559" style="display:none">One of the things that I have liked so much about the His Fair Assassins series, besides the Assassin Nuns of course is the <b>blending of completely fictionalized characters with actual historical events</b>. The time lines are not exact but the major events and characters are. <br /><br />Grave Mercy was more of a political intrigue, Dark Triumph an Adventure and now Mortal Heart is more of a Fantasy and love story. This book is far more invested into the lore of the gods Mortain in particular but the other Nine as well and their increasingly changing roles with the influx of the Christianity. I really liked how LaFever’s imagined the shift in this period of time and incorporated it with actual historical event. <br /><br />Annith has been in the Convent of Mortain for most of her life. She has dreamed of serving him and being Mortain’s handmaiden of death for as long as she can remember, she longs to get out of the convent and into the real world. But every one of her peers has been sent out before her and now even younger girls are being given assignments. When it becomes clear that the Abbess has plans for Annith to become the seeress for the convent and never leave she decides she has had enough and must take her life in her own hands.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Reverend Mother, I have spent my entire life training for one thing—to be Death’s handmaiden and carry out His will here on earth. At no time have I ever felt called to the duties that Sister Vereda performs.”</i>
</blockquote><br />The first 20% of the book is a little slow while Annith is at the convent. But once she leaves things get really interesting. Annith captures the attention and intense interest of Balthazaar, the leader of the Hellequin, Mortain’s army of the dead that hunts wicked or lost souls to return to the underworld.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“I am just overwhelmed by the immensity of Mortain’s grace. That even if we are lost or wandering, He will find us—always, He will find us—and try to bring us home.”<br />“Yes,” Balthazaar says. “He will.”<br />His finger lingers against my cheek a moment before he turns and walks away. As I watch him depart, I wonder if the hellequin are Mortain’s way of ensuring I find my way home, wherever that may be, and if Balthazaar’s words are a warning or a promise.</i>
</blockquote><br />Annith also finds out so much more about her past, the Abbess and her own role to play in helping Queen Anne and all of Brittany. It seems that the stories of the gods might have something in them that could give Anne a chance against the French.<br /><br />While I enjoyed the historical aspects of the story, this one in particular had more supernatural events going on. More about the gods and their past came into play. I liked how each order had their own stories and how each story held some truth to it but not the complete story. <br /><br />I don’t want to say too much about the love interest other than he was great and I really liked the way that whole storyline played out. Leader of the Hellequin he is dark, brooding and has a sense of sadness and longing to him. While most people are scared of the Hellequin Annith finds an easy rhythm while traveling with them and something starts to blossom between her and Balthazaar. LaFever’s really surprised me with the Hero of this story. Annith deserved an epic love and I think she got it in him.<br /><br />Mortal Heart gave me satisfactory endings to Ismae, Sybella and Annith’s stories. I know where all three girls will be at least for the next five years or so. I also really liked how Anne’s story played out. If you knew anything about the period in history you know what will eventually happen but I liked the way LaFever’s imagined getting there. <b>Fantastic re-telling of a historic period with some supernatural elements</b>.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2330784981217602559" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_344209865" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/344209865" />
    <a title="Alyssa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8472395-alyssa"><img alt="Alyssa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500935920p2/8472395.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/344209865?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alyssa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alyssa" href="/user/show/8472395-alyssa">Alyssa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8472395-alyssa?shelf=2014-releases">2014-releases</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer344209865" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer807217286815950152">***<a href='http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2014/10/review-mortal-heart-by-robin-lafevers.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Review posted on The Eater of Books! blog</a>***<br/><br/>Mortal Heart by Robin LaFevers<br/>Book Three of the His Fair Assassins series<br/>Publisher: HMH Books for Young Readers<br/>Publication Date: November 4, 2014<br/>Rating: 4 stars<br/>Source: ARC sent by the publisher<br/><br/>Summary (from Goodreads):<br/><br/>Annith has watched her gifted sisters at the convent come and go, carrying out their dark dealings in the name of St. Mortain, patiently awaiting her own turn to serve Death. But her worst fears are realized when she discovers she is b</span>
  <span id="freeText807217286815950152" style="display:none">***<a href="http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2014/10/review-mortal-heart-by-robin-lafevers.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Review posted on The Eater of Books! blog</a>***<br /><br />Mortal Heart by Robin LaFevers<br />Book Three of the His Fair Assassins series<br />Publisher: HMH Books for Young Readers<br />Publication Date: November 4, 2014<br />Rating: 4 stars<br />Source: ARC sent by the publisher<br /><br />Summary (from Goodreads):<br /><br />Annith has watched her gifted sisters at the convent come and go, carrying out their dark dealings in the name of St. Mortain, patiently awaiting her own turn to serve Death. But her worst fears are realized when she discovers she is being groomed by the abbess as a Seeress, to be forever sequestered in the rock and stone womb of the convent. Feeling sorely betrayed, Annith decides to strike out on her own.<br /><br />She has spent her whole life training to be an assassin. Just because the convent has changed its mind doesn't mean she has...<br /><br />What I Liked:<br /><br />It's officially official (again): this series is one of my favorite series everrrrrr. Grave Mercy was my favorite novel of 2012, and Dark Triumph was an excellent sequel (which I just read this past March). I preferred Ismae's story to Sybella's, but I just knew that I would love Annith's story.<br /><br />Annith has been in the convent, serving Mortain, longer than any of the other girls. She has never been on an assignment, whereas girls her age (like Ismae and Sybella) have been sent out. When Annith escapes, taking matters into her own hands, she discovers that some legends are true, and that she isn't quite like the other daughters of Mortain. Time is ticking for the duchess and the country, and Annith has an important role to play in the war to decide the ruling power of Europe.<br /><br />I love this series. I love that it appears to be a companion series, and it could be, but it really isn't. There are several general plots that run throughout the series - like the duchess and her marriage and the politics and the war and so much political scheming! Also, we get to see Ismae/Duval and Sybella/Beast in this book, as well as other characters from books one and two that I did not think would appear again.<br /><br />The first book is still my favorite of the series, but this book comes in second (with Dark Triumph in a close third). I love how complex this book is - it's not just about Annith and her self-discovery. The brewing war and overarching political conflict is also at the forefront of the book, as Annith is heading to Guérande (which is where Ismae, Duval, Sybella, etc. are). Annith has a key part to play in the war, but we don't get to see this until late in the book.<br /><br />The book is pretty long (450+ pages), but the story is so intriguing and fun to read. Maybe "fun" isn't the right word - I mean like, totally engrossing and engaging. I love Ismae/Duval, and I enjoyed reading about Sybella/Beast, and I really REALLY wanted to know more about Annith (and her love interest, who I will talk about later). We follow Annith from the convent to some crazy forest thing (no spoilers!) to where the duchess and Ismae/Sybella are, and there, Annith takes her place helping the duchess, but also, discovering secrets about the abbess, and her (Annith's) past.<br /><br />Annith is a mystery, for most of the book. We don't know who she is, or what she is, but we know that she cannot be an "ordinary" daughter of Mortain. She has no gifts of Mortain, but she is a faithful servant and a very skilled assassin. Annith is obedient, but there is always a thread of rebellion laced through her heart. She is determined to discover the truth of the abbess's schemes and plotting - and we know how twisted the abbess seemed in books one and two.<br /><br />Yes, yes there is romance in this book. The romance is a bit... unexpected, as LaFevers introduces a new element to the lore of the story. The male love interest in question is part of the new element of the story (which I won't give away). His name is Balthazaar, I'll give you that. I loveeeee Balthazaar - he is an interesting character, and has quite the dangerous edge. I like edgy. I won't say more. I thought it was interesting how LaFevers resolved the romance - I didn't know how it would end, honestly.<br /><br />This is probably my favorite historical fiction series in YA literature. Like, I loveee historical fiction, and I read a lot of it, but this has to be my favorite. Medieval historic times? Totally my thing. Plus all the politics and conflict AND breathtaking romance? Like woah.<br /><br />The ending of this book (and therefore, series) is good. I'm not going to say if it ended with a "happily ever after" or whatever - no spoilers from me! But it was good. I loved it. I love how things fit together. LaFevers addressed all of the conflicts in the book and series. Very well-done!<br /><br />Sufficient it to say, I was VERY pleased with this book. All the waiting and putting off reading this one despite having a review copy (I do things chronologically) was totally worth it. This book was stunning, beautifully written, solidly crafted, and all around, amazing!<br /><br />What I Did Not Like:<br /><br />Okay, I have to be honest, it took me a bit to get into the book. Maybe like, a hundred pages (or thereabout). It's a 450+ page book, so one hundred pages isn't really THAT much. Things get interesting when Annith leaves the convent, basically. Before that, I'm kind of like okay... I know LaFevers is setting up the scene, but eh. Necessary "evil".<br /><br />I don't really have many dislikes - this one just FEELS like a 4-star-read, you know? I loved Grave Mercy more, but I really liked this book! More like 4.5 stars.<br /><br />Would I Recommend It:<br /><br />I would recommend this book AND I would totally recommend this series in general! Seriously, this series is an Alyssa-approved series, one of my favorites (and probably my favorite YA historical fiction series). Plus, check out the covers! I like the original cover of Dark Triumph, but in general, I LOVED the covers of these books. And the books. <br /><br />Rating:<br /><br />4.5 stars -&gt; rounded down to 4 stars (only because it's not quite to 5 stars, like Grave Mercy. If that makes sense). But really guys, this book (and series) is so so so good! One of the best! </span>
  <a data-text-id="807217286815950152" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_616773672" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/616773672" />
    <a title="Alyssa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4152087-alyssa"><img alt="Alyssa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1395375020p2/4152087.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/616773672?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alyssa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alyssa" href="/user/show/4152087-alyssa">Alyssa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer616773672" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17703002416220658911">After falling in love with GRAVE MERCY and DARK TRIUMPH, I had high expectations for MORTAL HEART. Turns out I didn’t need to worry, this book exceeded my expectations and made an absolutely great conclusion to the epic His Fair Assassin trilogy.<br/><br/>Despite somewhat of a slow start, MORTAL HEART quickly picks as we get to know Annith a bit more. She was somewhat of a mystery in the previous books and the beginning of this one really focuses on answering some of the questions you might have had about</span>
  <span id="freeText17703002416220658911" style="display:none">After falling in love with GRAVE MERCY and DARK TRIUMPH, I had high expectations for MORTAL HEART. Turns out I didn’t need to worry, this book exceeded my expectations and made an absolutely great conclusion to the epic His Fair Assassin trilogy.<br><br>Despite somewhat of a slow start, MORTAL HEART quickly picks as we get to know Annith a bit more. She was somewhat of a mystery in the previous books and the beginning of this one really focuses on answering some of the questions you might have had about her, and we realize why she is the way she is. It wasn’t the most exciting or suspenseful bit, but it allows the reader to connect to Annith and really grow to care about her.<br><br>There are plenty of familiar faces but a whole heap of fresh ones as well, which is a nice surprise considering this is the final installment. I loved seeing returning characters and what they’ve been up to since we left them in the previous books. Speaking of new characters though…<br><br>The romance. So heartbreaking, so sweet, so dangerous, so awesome. If you fell in love with Duval and Beast, you just wait. Just when I thought there couldn’t be yet another amazing love interest in this series…<br><br>And guys, the twists. There was one I saw coming, but the other… The other…<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1414698890ra/11679430.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I loved the way it was revealed too. Chills. Serious chills. So good.<br><br>We learn so much more about everything in this book, discovering the truth just as Annith does. All of these revelations make me want to immediately go back and reread all the books, especially MORTAL HEART, with this new knowledge. Everything really comes together in the end, and there couldn’t be a more satisfying conclusion to this series.<br><br>LaFevers’ writing continues to impress, it is gorgeous. It’s not the type of writing that goes on and on to fill pages with endless prose, but is meaningful and really adds to the story as a whole. I want to include ALL THE QUOTES but they are pretty spoilery so I suggest getting to this series ASAP so we can gush about them. I’m sold on LaFevers’ storytelling, and I can’t wait to get my hands on whatever she writes next.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1414698890ra/11679431.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>This book was provided to me in exchange for an <b>honest</b> review.<br>None of these gifs are mine.</i></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_511635874" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/511635874" />
    <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library"><img alt="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350750103p2/4551536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/511635874?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=own-a-dtb">own-a-dtb</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=just-another-book-crush">just-another-book-crush</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=horrible-whiner">horrible-whiner</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=edelweiss">edelweiss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=i-see-dead-people">i-see-dead-people</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=are-you-kidding-me">are-you-kidding-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=failed-to-impress">failed-to-impress</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer511635874" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16292506617590909587">3.5 stars. <br/>When <i>Grave Mercy</i> first came out, it polarized opinions and caused some very heated discussions. Some felt that it focused too hard on the romance and others were disappointed by the number of deaths these killer nuns inflicted. Some, on the other hand, felt that it achieved a perfect balance between court politics, murder and romance. I myself was an immediately fell in love with the characters, all the court intrigue and the beautiful historical setting. <i>Dark Triumph</i> further confirme</span>
  <span id="freeText16292506617590909587" style="display:none">3.5 stars. <br>When <i>Grave Mercy</i> first came out, it polarized opinions and caused some very heated discussions. Some felt that it focused too hard on the romance and others were disappointed by the number of deaths these killer nuns inflicted. Some, on the other hand, felt that it achieved a perfect balance between court politics, murder and romance. I myself was an immediately fell in love with the characters, all the court intrigue and the beautiful historical setting. <i>Dark Triumph</i> further confirmed my opinion. It was much darker than its predecessor, incredibly painful and cruel to both Sybella and the reader, but it was also heart-wrenchingly beautiful and it made me feel unimaginable things.<br><br>Needless to say, I dreamed of getting my hands on <i>Mortal Heart</i>, desperate to learn Annith’s fate. But when it finally came and when I managed to read it, the emotional impact was not at all what I’d hoped for. Alas, I found myself feeling oddly indifferent.<br><br>There is nothing technically wrong with Annith’s story. LaFevers once again deserves praise for her gorgeous writing, her planning and her strong historical basis. She built an entire imaginary world around few vague historical facts and I think her idea, as well as her execution, is nothing short of admirable. <br><br>I felt, however, that after all the build-up inevitably caused by the previous two books, Annith’s character lacked the necessary strength to hold everything together. I liked Annith well enough, I suppose, but compared to Sybella or even Ismae, she somehow fades into the background. For me she never managed to become more than a fairly prominent secondary character. <br><br>My lack of connection with Annith caused a noticeable lack of connection with the romantic aspect of this book. Admittedly, Sybella and Beast were hard to live up to, but Annith’s romance came completely out of the blue and was far too outlandish for my taste. <br><br>Once the focus shifted away from Annith, though, the overall plot was executed perfectly. I admire LaFevers for keeping everything together and planning the main plotline so well while staying true to those few historical facts. It’s quite ingenuous and it makes me incredibly excited about her future projects, regardless of how I felt about this book. <br><br>As the author of my two all-time favorite reads, LaFevers firmly remains on my auto-buy list. While this book wasn’t at all what I’d hoped for, the trilogy as a whole is unforgettable and so very clever. If you haven’t already, I’d definitely give it a try.<br><br><br><a href="http://www.thenocturnallibrary.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380226536i/681142.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10260157322550892440">4.5<br/><br/>This is truly one of the best, most underrated historical fantasy-romance series EVER. I adore the historical background, the way the author manages to weave history, mythology and fantasy together so seamlessly to create a complete and convincing picture.<br/><br/>I adore the romances in these books, because even though they might become a little cliché at times, they always come with a good, empowering message and that tips the scales in favour of them far more than anything else could.<br/><br/>This was a won</span>
  <span id="freeText10260157322550892440" style="display:none">4.5<br /><br />This is truly one of the best, most underrated historical fantasy-romance series EVER. I adore the historical background, the way the author manages to weave history, mythology and fantasy together so seamlessly to create a complete and convincing picture.<br /><br />I adore the romances in these books, because even though they might become a little cliché at times, they always come with a good, empowering message and that tips the scales in favour of them far more than anything else could.<br /><br />This was a wonderful conclusion to the trilogy, that brought everything full circle and answered many of the open questions from the previous books. It was well written, suspenseful at times and most importantly, incredibly entertaining.<br /><br />Will forever be re-reading these books, for sure.</span>

<div id="review_602960640" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/602960640" />
    <a title="Keertana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana"><img alt="Keertana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438801223p2/7584700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/602960640?book_show_action=true">Apr 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Keertana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Keertana" href="/user/show/7584700-keertana">Keertana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer602960640" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15539390069139165411">To be frank, I don't have much to say about <i>Mortal Heart.</i> It's a satisfactory ending to LaFevers debut trilogy--and wraps up all the loose ends nicely--but as far as being Annith's story, I felt it lacking. Perhaps it's simply because Annith isn't as strong a force to be reckoned with as Sybella. It's not that Annith isn't a formidable assassin--because she is--and her force of will is to be respected as she struggles to find the truth within her beloved abbey. Yet, she doesn't possess Sybella o</span>
  <span id="freeText15539390069139165411" style="display:none">To be frank, I don't have much to say about <i>Mortal Heart.</i> It's a satisfactory ending to LaFevers debut trilogy--and wraps up all the loose ends nicely--but as far as being Annith's story, I felt it lacking. Perhaps it's simply because Annith isn't as strong a force to be reckoned with as Sybella. It's not that Annith isn't a formidable assassin--because she is--and her force of will is to be respected as she struggles to find the truth within her beloved abbey. Yet, she doesn't possess Sybella or Ismae's dark past which makes their stories compelling from the start itself and though it takes awhile for Annith's tale to find its footing, it continues to lose traction over time, not gain. I love Annith as a protagonist but the journey she undertakes in <i>Mortal Heart</i> pales in comparison to the stakes in both the previous novels. Moreover, the romance did absolutely <i>nothing</i> for me except to make me cringe a time or two and question--a lot--why there couldn't have been anyone else for Annith. <br /><br />I feel as if <i>Mortal Heart</i> is a tricky novel, being the final installment in this trilogy, and LaFevers succeeds in many ways. Not only does the plot line that began in <i>Grave Mercy</i> reach fruition, but we are able to see our three heroines united, changed, and happier than they were when we first met them. Unlike the last two novels, <i>Mortal Heart</i> doesn't revolve around an assassination or a <i>piece</i> of the plot; it's where the entire story converges into one. Thus, Annith isn't the sole starring character at hand. Though we follow <i>her</i> journey, there are other compelling, strong women at play who--and this just may be my personal love of Sybella--at times undermined Annith's casting into the spotlight. <br /><br />Additionally, though the romance isn't--and shouldn't be--a deciding factor in the enjoyment of a novel, I wasn't on board with this love story at any point and after Sybella and Beast's tale, felt vastly disappointed with this one. Frankly speaking, I didn't feel as if Annith needed romance. She's such a compelling and strong heroine, one whose loyalties to her sisters and friendships with them makes up so much of her being, that to have that replaced with a romance didn't hold the same weight or resonance for me as it likely should have. Plus, the romances of Ismae and Sybella, held side-by-side with Annith's lack of romance at first and then, later, her romantic interest, only made me feel as if Annith was desperate for the love Ismae and Sybella had found and needed a man to complete her as her sisters did. I have never felt that way about the romances in this series until this odd dichotomy.<br /><br /><i>Mortal Heart</i> brings up shocking revelations and I have no doubt that die-hard fans of this series will adore this final installment. As someone who didn't plan to continue the series after <i>Grave Mercy</i>--something about that book simply did not tick with me--yet fell in love with <i>Dark Triumph,</i> this final installment falls somewhere in the middle. Not nearly as good as <i>Dark Triumph</i> but far more satisfactory than <i>Grave Mercy.</i> LaFevers trilogy is a beloved one among many and though it doesn't rank among my favorites by far, I love these heroines and everything they stand for. Thus, I do not hesitate to recommend forth this series, flaws and all. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15539390069139165411" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1049338508" />

<span id="freeTextContainer11900329639085167774">This is the final book in the historical fantasy His Fair Assassin trilogy. Each book focused on a different "daughter of Mortain," or Handmaiden of Death. This was Annith's book. I liked it. Everything wrapped up nicely and everyone got their HEAs. I was surprised by several twists in this. This book wasn't as exciting as Sybella's book, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9943270.Dark_Triumph__His_Fair_Assassin___2_' title='Dark Triumph (His Fair Assassin, #2) by Robin LaFevers' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dark Triumph</a>, but it was still enjoyable. Annith was a pure soul who deserved to find the answers to her past and someone to love. I'm glad the truth about the</span>
  <span id="freeText11900329639085167774" style="display:none">This is the final book in the historical fantasy His Fair Assassin trilogy. Each book focused on a different "daughter of Mortain," or Handmaiden of Death. This was Annith's book. I liked it. Everything wrapped up nicely and everyone got their HEAs. I was surprised by several twists in this. This book wasn't as exciting as Sybella's book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9943270.Dark_Triumph__His_Fair_Assassin___2_" title="Dark Triumph (His Fair Assassin, #2) by Robin LaFevers" rel="nofollow noopener">Dark Triumph</a>, but it was still enjoyable. Annith was a pure soul who deserved to find the answers to her past and someone to love. I'm glad the truth about the Abbess came out and she was dealt with. It was nice to see the characters from the previous books back too. Everything ended in a satisfying way.</span>

<div id="review_1927367392" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1927367392" />
    <a title="Deborah Obida" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54790180-deborah-obida"><img alt="Deborah Obida" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604679377p2/54790180.jpg" /></a>

  <span id="freeText17758463175688277716" style="display:none">This series took the longest to finish, I started reading it in 2017 and finished in 2019, I read a book each year and am glad I splitted it.<br /><br />This book is my favourite in the series, Annith is also my favourite of all three girls, her story had so much revelations and its a great conclusion to the series.<br /><br /><u>World building and Writing </u><br />Before this series I had no idea the French invaded Brittany. The author did such an amazing job depicting it. There was no confusion whatsoever. The book like its predecessors its written in first person POV of Annith the MC.<br /><br /><u>Characters</u><br />Annith is such a strong female character and she is nothing like the way people thought her to be, she is no where near docile. She is brave and goes for what she wants.<br /><br />Balthazar the love interest is another great character, can't say much about him cause of spoilers. But one thingis for sure, he is kind, loving and selfless. What more could one ask for.<br /><br />Sybella, Isbeau, Duval and Beast were all in this and they all played interesting roles, even the Abbess. <br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer483369329299909120">This was a great ending to the 'His Fair Assassin' series. Everything was tied up really well, and I am glad to see Ismae, Sybella, and Annith all get a happy ending. I didn't enjoy this quite as much as the first two books. And it is definitely more of a fairytale than a historical fiction, in my opinion. Still, I loved this series very much and I am glad to have discovered it. </span>

<div id="review_1242266303" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1242266303" />
    <a title="Kristin Hackett (SuperSpaceChick)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5524572-kristin-hackett-superspacechick"><img alt="Kristin Hackett (SuperSpaceChick)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481980296p2/5524572.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1242266303?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristin Hackett (SuperSpaceChick)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristin Hackett (SuperSpaceChick)" href="/user/show/5524572-kristin-hackett-superspacechick">Kristin Hackett (SuperSpaceChick)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1242266303" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8834379838342206688">Originally posted on <a href='http://superspacechick.com/2017/03/07/tea-book-chat-mortal-heart-robin-lafevers-fair-assassin-3/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Super Space Chick</a>:<br/><br/>Personal Thoughts: I’m not quite sure why it took me so long to finally finish the His Fair Assassin’s trilogy. I really enjoyed Grave Mercy and Dark Triumph which I read last year but I hadn’t reached for Mortal Heart until very recently. Maybe I was worried about not having anymore to read once the story concluded but someone pointed out to me that we’re getting two more books set in the same world over the next couple of years so I suppose that’s why I f</span>
  <span id="freeText8834379838342206688" style="display:none">Originally posted on <a href="http://superspacechick.com/2017/03/07/tea-book-chat-mortal-heart-robin-lafevers-fair-assassin-3/" rel="nofollow noopener">Super Space Chick</a>:<br /><br />Personal Thoughts: I’m not quite sure why it took me so long to finally finish the His Fair Assassin’s trilogy. I really enjoyed Grave Mercy and Dark Triumph which I read last year but I hadn’t reached for Mortal Heart until very recently. Maybe I was worried about not having anymore to read once the story concluded but someone pointed out to me that we’re getting two more books set in the same world over the next couple of years so I suppose that’s why I felt ready to dive in! I was certain that none of the girl’s stories would top Ismae’s for me (Grave Mercy) but I actually think that Annith has taken her place as my new favorite.<br /><br />Plot Summary: Following the events of Grave Mercy and Dark Triumph, the tweenage Dutchess of Brittany is in quite the predicament. The French are threatening to take over Brittany and they’ve been sending their armies in for war. With the help of Ismae and Sybella, the Dutchess has been able to avoid several assassination attempts and attempts at usurping her but the situation is really coming to a head in this final installment which follows Annith, the last of the sisters never to be sent out on a mission by the convent so she takes matters into her own hands.<br /><br />Critique: Annith is by far one of the most interesting girls at the convent of Saint Mortain. As a handmaiden of death, she spent her entire life training to be sent out on a mission but time and time again she’s seen many of the girls, some much younger and less prepared than she be sent out while she’s stuck at the convent. The mysteries surrounding her birth and her relationship with the abbess and her predecessor is a complex web that is fascinating to watch unfold. I love that Annith takes matters into her own hands and despite always being the agreeable person she is, she really challenges authority, searches for truth and handles the revelations she discovers with a large amount of grace. She never loses sight of herself or her main objectives despite all of the questions that her past leaves her with. I also really loved the relationship between her and Balthazaar. Annith’s unwavering faith in Mortain is also something to be admired and I just loved where her storyline went because it diverged far away from what I had been expecting. I also think Mortal Heart is my favorite of the series because we get to see Annith, Ismae and Sybella reunited and there are so many heartwarming moments between these sisters. Everything plays out nicely and the story is completely tied up upon the completion of the novel but there are enough questions that the further installments will definitely be high upon my TBR list!<br /><br />Do I Recommend?: Oh yes! But you must start with Grave Mercy and work your way to Mortal Heart first! If you like historical fiction with an element of fantasy and appreciate 15th century jokes, this is the book for you!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8834379838342206688" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="christina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6799093-christina"><img alt="christina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1467899062p2/6799093.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2437685839?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="christina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="christina" href="/user/show/6799093-christina">christina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780544542570" href="/book/show/23719418-mortal-heart">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6799093-christina?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6799093-christina?shelf=ya-series">ya-series</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2437685839" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11853224452573677790">Overall this was a good resolution to this part of the series and I cannot wait to read the new duology featuring Sybella and Beast in France! <br/><br/>So this book was definitely giving off some Hades & Persephone vibes for sure, with a dash of Artemis because Annith is not no DNB - she out here killing doodz, and I was totally here for it.<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1532530549i/26026999.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I really like how different all 3 girls are in each book, in book 1 Ismae sometimes gives off some Mary Sue vibes, but even she really grows into this dynamic woman. </span>
  <span id="freeText11853224452573677790" style="display:none">Overall this was a good resolution to this part of the series and I cannot wait to read the new duology featuring Sybella and Beast in France! <br><br>So this book was definitely giving off some Hades &amp; Persephone vibes for sure, with a dash of Artemis because Annith is not no DNB - she out here killing doodz, and I was totally here for it.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1532530549i/26026999.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I really like how different all 3 girls are in each book, in book 1 Ismae sometimes gives off some Mary Sue vibes, but even she really grows into this dynamic woman. As for Sybella, she is a bad ass bitch that I would die for. It's also worth mentioning that although all 3 girls are very different with their own paths, they love and support each other. Even when they are jealous or have their differences they stick together. Which is so refreshing, can I get an AMEN?<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1522426309ra/25297909.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Some of the "twists" in the plot were pretty obvious, but still nicely done. I think the revelations about the Abbess were kind of blah though, and didn't really explain all of her actions well. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Like she was obviously insane, but to go through all of that torment for so many years and murder everyone to get to the top, only to throw it all away by getting caught in schemes with Annith's father Crunard, was just dumb. She could have played her hand so much better. It was just not believable that she would be able to pull off that stunt for so long, so flawlessly, only to get super sloppy at the end. Maybe it was her fear of not being able to protect her only daughter, Annith once she was of age and that drove her into a mad frenzy and caused her to start making mistakes? ¯\_(ツ)_/¯<br>I guess I'm just glad she was at least punished for her wrong doings, and that Annith didn't allow herself to be manipulated by either of her "parents". <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>As for the love story, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I was here for Annith being with Mortain God of Death, and even though his identity was "hidden" at first, I think it helped the romance blossom. Annith riding with The Hunt was probably my favorite part of the story, and I would like to see more of her and Mortain working together. I also liked that both Ismae and Sybella had different reactions to the revelation of the romance, Ismae being a little "I don't know, that's our dad and you thought he was your dad, but I want you to be happy" to Sybella being like "yo my brothers wanted to do me, sooo no judgement here girl!" <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>I was worried that Annith being introduced as the "goody two shoes" girl was going to make this installment boring, but Annith really stepped up. She made her own decisions, forged her own destiny, and I was super proud of her by the end of it.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1532530549i/26027000._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Overall, I really enjoyed this series -even though I wished it would get a little darker and sexier at times. However, I get that this is supposed to be YA and I understand why the author held back some. I'm hoping that the next duology will be a little more bad ass with a dash of spice. ⚔️🔥☠️<br><br>------------------------<br><br><b>His Fair Assassin Trilogy</b><br>Grave Mercy, #1 ★★★★☆<br>Dark Triumph, #2 ★★★★☆<br>Mortal Heart, #3 ★★★★☆<br><br><b>Courting Darkness Duology</b><br>Courting Darkness, #1 ★★★☆☆<br>Igniting Darkness, #2 ★★★★☆</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
